<p><b>Ayman Mohammed Rabie al-Zawahiri</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">أيمن محمد ربيع الظواهري</span>‎‎<span class="nowrap">  </span><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="DIN 31635 Arabic">ʾAyman Muḥammad Rabīʿ aẓ-Ẓawāhirī</span></i>, born June 19, 1951)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FBI_Most_Wanted_Terrorists_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FBI_Most_Wanted_Terrorists-5">[5]</a></sup> is the current leader of <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> and a current<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc16jun11_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc16jun11-6">[6]</a></sup> or former member and senior official of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamist" title="Islamist">Islamist</a> organizations which have orchestrated and carried out attacks in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>. In 2012, he called on Muslims to kidnap Western tourists in Muslim countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department" title="U.S. State Department">U.S. State Department</a> has offered a <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>25 million reward for information leading to al-Zawahiri's capture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> He is under worldwide sanctions by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_1267_Committee" title="United Nations Security Council 1267 Committee">United Nations Security Council 1267 Committee</a> as a member or affiliate of al-Qaeda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refUN_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-refUN-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternate_names_and_sobriquets">Alternate names and sobriquets</span></h2>
<p>Ayman Mohammed Rabie al-Zawahiri is pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Arabic" title="Help:IPA for Arabic">[ˈʔæjmæn mʊˈħæmːæd rɑˈbiːʕ azˤːɑˈwæːhɪriː]</a></span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Arabic" title="Help:IPA for Arabic">[aðˤːɑˈwæːhɪriː]</a></span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>. Zawahiri is usually spelled Zawahri (from the pronunciation in his native <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Arabic" title="Egyptian Arabic">Egyptian Arabic</a>), but is sometimes spelled "Dhawahri" if transliterated directly from Modern Standard Arabic, also called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literary_Arabic" title="Literary Arabic">Literary Arabic</a>, in certain academic circles. Using the Intelligence Community Standard for the Transliteration of Arabic Names, it is spelled Zawahri.</p>
<p>Al-Zawahiri has also gone under following names:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FBI_Al-Zawahiri_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FBI_Al-Zawahiri-10">[10]</a></sup> <b>Abu Muhammad</b> / <b>Abu Mohammed</b> (أبو محمّد), <b>Abu Fatima</b> (أبو فاطمة), <b>Muhammad Ibrahim</b> (محمّد إبراهيم), <b>Abu Abdallah</b> (أبو عبدالله), <b>Abu al-Mu'iz</b> (أبو المعز), <b>The Doctor</b>, <b>The Teacher</b>, <b>Nur</b> (نور), <b>Ustaz</b> (أستاذ), <b>Abu Mohammed Nur al-Deen</b> (أبو محمّد نورالدين), <b>Abdel Muaz</b> / <b>Abdel Moez</b> / <b>Abdel Muez</b> (عبدالمعز).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h3>
<p>Ayman al-Zawahiri was born in 1951 in the neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Maadi" title="Maadi">Maadi</a>, Cairo, the Kingdom of Egypt, to Mohammed Rabie al-Zawahiri and Umayma Azzam. The al-Zawahiri family was considered "<a href="/wiki/Upper_middle_class" title="Upper middle class">upper middle class</a>" while they lived in <a href="/wiki/Maadi" title="Maadi">Maadi</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Al-Zawahiri's parents both came from prosperous families. Al-Zawahiri's father, Mohammed Rabie al-Zawahiri, came from a large family of doctors and scholars. Mohammed Rabie became a <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeon</a> and a medical professor at <a href="/wiki/Cairo_University" title="Cairo University">Cairo University</a>. Ayman's mother, Umayma Azzam, came from a wealthy, politically active clan. Ayman has said that he has a deep affection for his mother. Her brother, Mahfouz Azzam, became a role model for Ayman as a teenager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Ayman has a younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Zawahiri" title="Muhammad al-Zawahiri">Muhammad al-Zawahiri</a>, and a twin sister, Heba Mohamed al-Zawahiri.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Al-Zawahiri's sister, Heba Mohamed al-Zawahiri, became a professor of <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">medical oncology</a> at <a href="/wiki/National_Cancer_Institute_Egypt" title="National Cancer Institute Egypt">the National Cancer Institute, Cairo University</a>. She described her brother as "silent and shy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Al-Zawahiri's brother, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Zawahiri" title="Muhammad al-Zawahiri">Muhammad al-Zawahiri</a>, was sent to the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> by his older brother in 1993. Ayman al-Zawahiri sent Muhammad to meet with <a href="/wiki/Alija_Izetbegovi%C4%87" title="Alija Izetbegović">Alija Izetbegović</a>, commander of the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Corps_of_the_Army_of_the_Republic_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="3rd Corps of the Army of the Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina">3rd Corps of the Army of the Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, along with senior staff officers attached and religious leaders, to check the Islamisation of the Bosnian Army and the funds received for the mujahedeen fighters in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnia" title="Bosnia">Bosnia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Muhammad was known as a <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistics</a> expert and is said to be the military commander of <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">Islamic Jihad</a>. Muhammad worked in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnia" title="Bosnia">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> under the cover of being an <a href="/wiki/International_Islamic_Relief_Organization" title="International Islamic Relief Organization">International Islamic Relief Organization</a> (IIRO) official. While hiding in the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, he was arrested in 2000, then extradited to Egypt, where he was sentenced to death. He was held in <a href="/wiki/Tora_Prison" title="Tora Prison">Tora Prison</a> in Cairo as a political detainee. Security officials said he was the head of the Special Action Committee of <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Islamic Jihad</a>, which organized terrorist operations. However, after the Egyptian popular uprising in the spring of 2011, on 17 March 2011 he was released from prison by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_the_Armed_Forces" title="Supreme Council of the Armed Forces">Supreme Council of the Armed Forces</a>, the interim government of Egypt. His lawyer said he had been held to extract information about his brother Ayman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> However, on 20 March 2011, he was re-arrested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> On 17 August 2013, Egyptian authorities arrested Muhammad al-Zawahiri at his home in <a href="/wiki/Giza" title="Giza">Giza</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ayman al-Zawahiri was reportedly a studious youth. Ayman excelled in school, loved poetry, and "hated violent sports" —which he thought were "inhumane." Al-Zawahiri studied medicine at <a href="/wiki/Cairo_University" title="Cairo University">Cairo University</a> and graduated in 1974 with <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_grading_in_Egypt" title="Academic grading in Egypt">gayyid giddan</a></i>. Following that he served three years as a surgeon in the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Army" title="Egyptian Army">Egyptian Army</a> after which he established a clinic near his parents in Maadi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wrightp42_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-wrightp42-17">[17]</a></sup> In 1978, he also earned a <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a> in <a href="/wiki/Surgery" title="Surgery">surgery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Ayman al-Zawahiri has also shown a radical understanding of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_theology" title="Islamic theology">Islamic theology</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_history" title="Islamic history">Islamic history</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> He speaks <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>.</p>
<p>Al-Zawahiri participated in <a href="/wiki/Youth_activism" title="Youth activism">Youth activism</a> as a student. He became both quite pious and political, under the influence of his uncle Mahfouz Azzam, and lecturer Mostafa Kamel Wasfi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monty_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-monty-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sayyid_Qutb" title="Sayyid Qutb">Sayyid Qutb</a> preached that to restore Islam and free Muslims, a vanguard of true Muslims modeling itself after the original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Companions_of_the_Prophet" title="Companions of the Prophet">Companions of the Prophet</a> had to be developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the age of 14, al-Zawahiri had joined the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a>. The following year the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_government" title="Egyptian government">Egyptian government</a> executed Qutb for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(political)" title="Conspiracy (political)">conspiracy</a>, and al-Zawahiri, along with four other secondary school students, helped form an "underground cell devoted to overthrowing the government and establishing an Islamist state." It was at this early age that al-Zawahiri developed a mission in life, "to put <a href="/wiki/Sayyid_Qutb" title="Sayyid Qutb">Qutb</a>'s vision into action."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> His cell eventually merged with others to form al-Jihad or <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wrightp42_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-wrightp42-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_children">Marriage and children</span></h3>
<p>Ayman al-Zawahiri has been married at least four times. His wives include Azza Ahmed Nowari and Umaima Hassan.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1978, al-Zawahiri married his first wife, Azza Ahmed Nowari, a student at Cairo University who was studying <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monty_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-monty-21">[21]</a></sup> Their wedding, which was held at the Continental Hotel in Opera Square,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monty_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-monty-21">[21]</a></sup> was very conservative, with separate areas for both men and women, and no music, photographs, or light-hearted humour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Many years later, when the United States attacked Afghanistan following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> in October 2001, Azza apparently had no idea that al-Zawahiri had supposedly been a <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihadi</a> emir (commander) for the last decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In June 2012, one of Zawahiri's four wives, Umaima Hassan, released a statement on the internet congratulating the role played by Muslim <a href="/wiki/Women_in_the_Arab_Spring" title="Women in the Arab Spring">women in the Arab Spring</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Al-Zawahiri and his wife Azza had four daughters, Fatima (born 1981), Umayma (born 1983), Nabila (born 1986), and Khadiga (born 1987), and a son, Mohammed (also born in 1987; the twin brother of Khadiga), who was a "delicate, well-mannered boy" and "the pet of his older sisters," subject to teasing and <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullying</a> in a traditional all-male environment, who preferred to "stay at home and help his mother."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1997, ten years after the birth of Mohammed, Azza gave birth to their fifth daughter, Aisha, who had <a href="/wiki/Down_syndrome" title="Down syndrome">Down syndrome</a>. In February 2004, <a href="/wiki/Abu_Zubaydah" title="Abu Zubaydah">Abu Zubaydah</a> was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterboarded" title="Waterboarded">waterboarded</a> and subsequently stated that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_Turab_Al-Urduni" title="Abu Turab Al-Urduni">Abu Turab Al-Urduni</a> had married one of al-Zawahiri's daughters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the first half of 2005, one of Al-Zawahiri's three surviving wives gave birth to a daughter, named Nawwar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berg_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-berg-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ayman al-Zawahiri's first wife Azza and two of their six children, Mohammad and Aisha, were killed in an air strike on <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> by US forces in late December 2001, following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> on the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn:_Jihadist_websites_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn:_Jihadist_websites-31">[31]</a></sup> After an American aerial bombardment of a Taliban-controlled building at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gardez,_Afghanistan" title="Gardez, Afghanistan">Gardez</a>, Azza was pinned under debris of a guesthouse roof. Concerned for her modesty, she "refused to be excavated" because "men would see her face" and she died from her injuries the following day. Her son, Mohammad, was also killed outright in the same house. Her four-year-old daughter with Down syndrome, Aisha, had not been hurt by the bombing, but died from exposure in the cold night while Afghan rescuers tried to save Azza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<p>Ayman al-Zawahiri worked in the medical field as a <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeon</a>. In 1985, al-Zawahiri went to Saudi Arabia on <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> and stayed to practice medicine in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a> for a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> As a reportedly qualified surgeon, when his organization merged with bin Laden's al-Qaeda, he became bin Laden's personal advisor and physician. He had first met bin Laden in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a> in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atkins2011_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atkins2011-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1981, Ayman al-Zawahiri also traveled to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peshawar,_Pakistan" title="Peshawar, Pakistan">Peshawar, Pakistan</a>, where he worked in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Crescent" title="Red Crescent">Red Crescent</a> hospital treating wounded refugees. There he became friends with the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Khadr" title="Ahmed Khadr">Ahmed Khadr</a>, and the two shared a number of conversations about the need for Islamic government and the needs of the Afghan people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-child_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-child-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993, al-Zawahiri traveled to the United States, where he addressed several <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> under his <i>Abdul Mu'iz</i> pseudonym, relying on his credentials from the Kuwaiti <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Crescent</a> to raise money for Afghan children who had been injured by Soviet <a href="/wiki/Land_mine" title="Land mine">land mines</a>—he only raised $2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Militant_activity">Militant activity</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assassination_plots">Assassination plots</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span></h4>
<p>In 1981, Al-Zawahiri was one of hundreds arrested following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assassination_of_President_Anwar_Sadat" title="Assassination of President Anwar Sadat">assassination of President Anwar Sadat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Initially, the plan was derailed when authorities were alerted to Al-Jihad's plan by the arrest of an operative carrying crucial information, in February 1981. President <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">Sadat</a> ordered the roundup of more than 1500 people, including many Al-Jihad members, but missed a cell in the military led by Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Islambouli" title="Khalid Islambouli">Khalid Islambouli</a>, who succeeded in assassinating Sadat during a military parade that October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> His lawyer, <a href="/wiki/Montasser_el-Zayat" title="Montasser el-Zayat">Montasser el-Zayat</a>, said that Zawahiri was tortured in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his book, <i>Al-Zawahiri as I Knew Him</i>, Al-Zayat maintains that under torture by the Egyptian police, following his arrest in connection with the murder of Sadat in 1981, Al-Zawahiri revealed the hiding place of <a href="/wiki/Essam_al-Qamari" title="Essam al-Qamari">Essam al-Qamari</a>, a key member of the Maadi cell of al-Jihad, which led to Al-Qamari's "arrest and eventual execution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993, al-Zawahiri's and <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">EIJ</a>'s connection with <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> may have led to a suicide bombing in an attempt on the life of <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Egypt)" title="Ministry of Interior (Egypt)">Egyptian Interior Minister</a> Hasan al-Alfi, the man heading the effort to quash the campaign of Islamist killings in Egypt. It failed, as did an attempt to assassinate Egyptian prime minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atef_Sidqi" title="Atef Sidqi">Atef Sidqi</a> three months later. The bombing of Sidqi's car injured 21 Egyptians and killed a young schoolgirl, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shayma_Abdel-Halim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shayma Abdel-Halim (page does not exist)">Shayma Abdel-Halim</a>. It followed two years of killings by another Islamist group, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Gama%27a_al-Islamiyya" title="Al-Gama'a al-Islamiyya">al-Gama'a al-Islamiyya</a>, that had killed over 200 people. Her funeral became a public spectacle, with her coffin carried through the streets of <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> and crowds shouting, "Terrorism is the enemy of God!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wright186_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wright186-42">[42]</a></sup> The police arrested 280 more of al-Jihad's members and executed six.</p>
<p>For their leading role in anti-Egyptian Government attacks in the 1990s, al-Zawahiri and his brother Muhammad al-Zawahiri were sentenced to death in the 1999 Egyptian case of the <a href="/wiki/Returnees_from_Albania" title="Returnees from Albania">Returnees from Albania</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span></h4>
<p>The 1995 <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_the_Egyptian_Embassy_in_Pakistan" title="Attack on the Egyptian Embassy in Pakistan">attack on the Egyptian embassy in Islamabad</a>, Pakistan, was the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</a>'s first success under Zawahiri's leadership, but Bin Laden had disapproved of the operation. The bombing alienated Pakistan, which was "the best route into Afghanistan".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="incomplete and run-on sentence, needs rewrite including source of quote. (May 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In July 2007, Al-Zawahiri supplied direction for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lal_Masjid_siege" title="Lal Masjid siege">Lal Masjid siege</a>, codename Operation Silence. This was the first confirmed time that Al-Zawahiri was taking militant steps against the Pakistan Government and guiding Islamic militants against the State of Pakistan. The <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Army" title="Pakistan Army">Pakistan Army</a> troops and Special Service Group taking control of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Mosque" title="Red Mosque">Red Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a> found letters from al-Zawahiri directing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_militants" title="Islamic militants">Islamic militants</a> <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Rashid_Ghazi" title="Abdul Rashid Ghazi">Abdul Rashid Ghazi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdul_Aziz_Ghazi" title="Abdul Aziz Ghazi">Abdul Aziz Ghazi</a>, who ran the mosque and adjacent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrasah" title="Madrasah">madrasah</a>. This conflict resulted in 100 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 27, 2007, al-Zawahiri was also implicated in the assassination of former Pakistani Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto" title="Benazir Bhutto">Benazir Bhutto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sudan">Sudan</span></h4>
<p>In 1994, the sons of <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Salama_Mabruk" title="Ahmad Salama Mabruk">Ahmad Salama Mabruk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Sharaf" title="Mohammed Sharaf">Mohammed Sharaf</a> were executed under al-Zawahiri's leadership for betraying <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</a>; the militants were ordered to leave the Sudan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span></h4>
<p>In 1998, Ayman al-Zawahiri was listed as under indictment<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indicted_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-indicted-48">[48]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> for his role in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1998_U.S._embassy_bombings" title="1998 U.S. embassy bombings">1998 U.S. embassy bombings</a>, a series of attacks that occurred on August 7, 1998, in which hundreds of people were killed in simultaneous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Truck_bomb" title="Truck bomb">truck bomb</a> explosions at the United States <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embassy" title="Embassy">embassies</a> in the major East African cities of <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>, Tanzania and <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FBI_Most_Wanted_Terrorists_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-FBI_Most_Wanted_Terrorists-5">[5]</a></sup> The attacks brought Osama bin Laden and Ayman al-Zawahiri to international attention.</p>
<p>In 2000, the <a href="/wiki/USS_Cole_bombing" title="USS Cole bombing">USS <i>Cole</i> bombing</a> encouraged several members to depart. <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Atef" title="Mohammed Atef">Mohammed Atef</a> went to escape Kandahar, Zawahiri to Kabul, and Bin Laden fled to Kabul, later joining Atef when he realised no American reprisal attacks were forthcoming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 10, 2001, al-Zawahiri appeared on the initial list of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a>'s top 22 <a href="/wiki/FBI_Most_Wanted_Terrorists" title="FBI Most Wanted Terrorists">Most Wanted Terrorists</a>, which was released to the public by U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>. In early November 2001, the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> government announced they were bestowing official Afghan <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a> on him, as well as Bin Laden, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Atef" title="Mohammed Atef">Mohammed Atef</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saif_al-Adl" title="Saif al-Adl">Saif al-Adl</a>, and Shaykh <a href="/wiki/Asim_Abdulrahman" title="Asim Abdulrahman">Asim Abdulrahman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizations">Organizations</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</span></h4>
<p>Ayman al-Zawahiri was previously the second and last "<a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">emir</a>" of the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</a>, having succeeded <a href="/wiki/Abbud_al-Zumar" title="Abbud al-Zumar">Abbud al-Zumar</a> in the latter role when Egyptian authorities sentenced al-Zumar to <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment" title="Life imprisonment">life imprisonment</a>. Ayman al-Zawahiri eventually became one of <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</a>'s leading organizers and recruiters. Zawahiri's hope was to recruit military officers and accumulate weapons, waiting for the right moment to launch "a complete overthrow of the existing order."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wrightp49_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-wrightp49-51">[51]</a></sup> Chief strategist of Al-Jihad was Aboud al-Zumar, a colonel in the military intelligence whose plan was to kill the main leaders of the country, capture the headquarters of the army and State Security, the telephone exchange building, and of course the radio and television building, where news of the Islamic revolution would then be broadcast, unleashing – he expected – "a popular uprising against secular authority all over the country."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wrightp49_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-wrightp49-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maktab_al-Khadamat">Maktab al-Khadamat</span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Peshawar" title="Peshawar">Peshawar</a>, he met up with <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>, who was running a base for <i><a href="/wiki/Mujahideen" title="Mujahideen">mujahideen</a></i> called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maktab_al-Khadamat" title="Maktab al-Khadamat">Maktab al-Khadamat</a> (MAK); founded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Yusuf_Azzam" title="Abdullah Yusuf Azzam">Abdullah Yusuf Azzam</a>. The radical position of al-Zawahiri and the other militants of Al-Jihad put them at odds with Sheikh Azzam, with whom they competed for bin Laden's financial resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Zawahiri carried two false passports, a Swiss one in the name of Amin Uthman and a Dutch one in the name of Mohmud Hifnawi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csisJaballah_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-csisJaballah-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI">FBI</a> agent <a href="/wiki/Ali_Soufan" title="Ali Soufan">Ali Soufan</a> mentioned in his book <i>The Black Banners</i> that Ayman al-Zawahiri is suspected of being behind Azzam's assassination in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rulit.net_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-rulit.net-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ayman_al-Zawahiri.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="366" data-file-width="277" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Ayman_al-Zawahiri.png/200px-Ayman_al-Zawahiri.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Ayman_al-Zawahiri.png 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ayman_al-Zawahiri.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This image used by the FBI shows Ayman al-Zawahiri in Khost, Afghanistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1998, al-Zawahiri formally merged the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</a> into al-Qaeda. According to reports by a former al-Qaeda member, he has worked in the al-Qaeda organization since its inception and was a senior member of the group's <i><a href="/wiki/Shura" title="Shura">shura</a></i> council. He was often described as a "lieutenant" to Osama bin Laden, though bin Laden's chosen biographer has referred to him as the "real brains" of al-Qaeda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSM1_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-CSM1-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 23, 1998, al-Zawahiri issued a joint <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatw%C4%81" title="Fatwā">fatwa</a> with <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> under the title "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Islamic_Front" title="World Islamic Front">World Islamic Front Against Jews and Crusaders</a>". Zawahiri, not bin Laden, is thought to have been the actual author of the fatwa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bin Laden and Al-Zawahiri organized an al-Qaeda congress on June 24, 1998. A week prior to the beginning of the conference, a group of well-armed assistants to al-Zawahiri had left by jeeps in the direction of Herat. Following the instructions of their patron, in the town of Koh-i-Doshakh they met three unknown Slavic-looking men who had arrived from Russia via Iran. After their arrival in Kandahar, they split up. One of the Russians was directly escorted to al-Zawahiri and he did not participate in the conference. The Western intelligence succeeded in acquiring photographs of him, but he disappeared for six years. According to Axis Globe, in 2004, when Qatar and U.S. investigated Russian embassy officials whom the United Arab Emirates had arrested in connection to the murder of <a href="/wiki/Zelimkhan_Yandarbiyev" title="Zelimkhan Yandarbiyev">Zelimkhan Yandarbiyev</a> in Qatar, computer software precisely established that a man who had walked to the Russian embassy in Doha was the same one who visited al-Zawahiri prior to the Al-Qaida conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergence_as_al-Qaeda.27s_chief_commander">Emergence as al-Qaeda's chief commander</span></h5>
<p>On April 30, 2009, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department" title="U.S. State Department">U.S. State Department</a> reported that al-Zawahiri had emerged as <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>'s operational and strategic commander<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ay1le_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ay1le-60">[60]</a></sup> and that Osama bin Laden was now only the ideological figurehead of the organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ay1le_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ay1le-60">[60]</a></sup> However, after the 2011 death of Osama, a senior U.S. intelligence official was quoted as saying intelligence gathered in the raid showed that bin Laden remained deeply involved in planning: “This compound (where bin Laden was killed) in <a href="/wiki/Abbottabad" title="Abbottabad">Abbottabad</a> was an active command-and-control center for al-Qaeda’s leader. He was active in operational planning and in driving tactical decisions within al-Qaeda.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-null_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-null-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the death of bin Laden, former Deputy National Security Advisor for Combating Terrorism <a href="/wiki/Juan_Zarate" title="Juan Zarate">Juan Zarate</a> said that al-Zawahiri would "clearly assume the mantle of leadership" of al-Qaeda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zarate_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-zarate-62">[62]</a></sup> But a senior U.S. administration official said that although al-Zawahiri was likely to be al-Qaeda's next leader, his authority was not "universally accepted" among al-Qaeda's followers, particularly in the Gulf region. Zarate said that al-Zawahiri was more controversial and less charismatic than bin Laden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rashad_Mohammad_Ismail&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rashad Mohammad Ismail (page does not exist)">Rashad Mohammad Ismail</a> (AKA "Abu Al-Fida"), a leading member of <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Arabian_Peninsula" title="Al-Qaeda in the Arabian Peninsula">al-Qaeda in the Arabian Peninsula</a>, stated that al-Zawahiri was the best candidate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hamid_Mir" title="Hamid Mir">Hamid Mir</a> is reported to have said that he believed that Ayman al-Zawahiri was the operational head of al-Qaeda, and that "[h]e is the person who can do the things that happened on Sept. 11."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSM1_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-CSM1-57">[57]</a></sup> Within days of the attacks, Zawahiri's name was put forward as Bin Laden's second-in-command, with reports suggesting he represented "a more formidable US foe than bin Laden."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_appointment">Formal appointment</span></h5>
<p>As of May 2, 2011, he became the leader of <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden" title="Death of Osama bin Laden">death of Osama bin Laden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zarate_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-zarate-62">[62]</a></sup> This was confirmed by a press release from al-Qaeda's general command on June 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc16jun11_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc16jun11-6">[6]</a></sup> al-Zawahiri's succession to command of <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> was announced on several of their websites on June 16, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn:_Jihadist_websites_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn:_Jihadist_websites-31">[31]</a></sup> On the same day, al-Qaeda renewed its position that <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> was an illegitimate state and that it wouldn't accept any compromise on <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-no_compromise_on_Palestine_or_Israel_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-no_compromise_on_Palestine_or_Israel-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The delayed announcement led some analysts to speculate that there was quarreling within al-Qaeda: "It doesn't suggest a vast reservoir of accumulated goodwill for him," said one celebrity journalist on <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quarreling_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-quarreling-67">[67]</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">U.S. Secretary of Defense</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gates" title="Robert Gates">Robert Gates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff">Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_Mullen" title="Mike Mullen">Mike Mullen</a> maintain that the delay didn't signal any kind of dispute within al-Qaeda,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gates_and_Mullen_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gates_and_Mullen-68">[68]</a></sup> and Mullen reiterated U.S. death threats toward al-Zawahiri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-renewing_pledge_to_kill_head_of_al-Qaeda_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-renewing_pledge_to_kill_head_of_al-Qaeda-69">[69]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> officials within the <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Obama</a> administration and Robert Gates, al-Zawahiri would find the leadership difficult as, while intelligent, he lacks combat experience and the charisma of <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gates_and_Mullen_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gates_and_Mullen-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Imprisonment">Imprisonment</span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt_2">Egypt</span></h5>
<p>Al-Zawahiri was convicted of dealing in weapons and received a three-year sentence, which he completed in 1984, shortly after his conviction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span></h5>
<p>At some point in 1994, al-Zawahiri was said to have "become a phantom"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wrightp250_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-wrightp250-73">[73]</a></sup> but is thought to have traveled widely to "Switzerland and <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>". A fake passport he was using shows that he traveled to <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 1, 1996, <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Salama_Mabruk" title="Ahmad Salama Mabruk">Ahmad Salama Mabruk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_Hisham_al-Hennawi" title="Mahmud Hisham al-Hennawi">Mahmud Hisham al-Hennawi</a> – both carrying false passports – accompanied al-Zawahiri on a trip to <a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechnya</a>, where they hoped to re-establish the faltering Jihad. Their leader was traveling under the name <i>Abdullah Imam Mohammed Amin</i>, and trading on his medical credentials for legitimacy. The group switched vehicles three times, but were arrested within hours of entering Russian territory and spent five months in a <a href="/wiki/Makhachkala" title="Makhachkala">Makhachkala</a> prison awaiting trial. The trio pleaded innocence, maintaining their disguise and having other al-Jihad members from <i>Bavari-C</i> send the Russian authorities pleas for leniency for their "merchant" colleagues who had been wrongly arrested; and Russian Member of Parliament <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nadyr_Khachiliev&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nadyr Khachiliev (page does not exist)">Nadyr Khachiliev</a> echoed the pleas for their speedy release as al-Jihad members <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Eidarous" title="Ibrahim Eidarous">Ibrahim Eidarous</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tharwat_Salah_Shehata" title="Tharwat Salah Shehata">Tharwat Salah Shehata</a> traveled to <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a> to plead for their release. Shehata received permission to visit the prisoners, and is believed to have smuggled them $3000 which was later confiscated from their cell, and to have given them a letter which the Russians didn't bother to translate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instead_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-instead-75">[75]</a></sup> In April 1997, the trio were sentenced to six months, and were subsequently released a month later and ran off without paying their court-appointed attorney Abulkhalik Abdusalamov his $1,800 legal fee citing their "poverty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instead_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-instead-75">[75]</a></sup> Shehata was sent on to Chechnya, where he met with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_Khattab" title="Ibn Khattab">Ibn Khattab</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wrightp250_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-wrightp250-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instead_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-instead-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leaving_Egypt">Leaving Egypt</span></h3>
<p>During this time, al-Zawahiri also began reconstituting the Egyptian Islamic Jihad (EIJ) along with other exiled militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The group had "very loose ties to their nominal imprisoned leader, Abud al-Zumur."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In Peshwar, al-Zawahiri is thought to have become radicalized by other Al-Jihad members, abandoning his old strategy of a swift coup d'état to change society from above, and embracing the idea of <a href="/wiki/Takfir" title="Takfir">takfir</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In 1991, EIJ broke with al-Zumur, and al-Zawahiri grabbed "the reins of power" to become EIJ leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_in_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran">Activities in the Islamic Republic of Iran</span></h3>
<p>Zawahiri has allegedly worked with the Islamic Republic of Iran on behalf of al-Qaeda. Lawrence Wright reports that EIJ operative Ali Mohammed "told the FBI that al-Jihad had planned a coup in Egypt in 1990." Zawahiri had studied the 1979 Islamist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_Revolution" title="Islamic Revolution">Islamic Revolution</a> and "sought training from the Iranians" as to how to duplicate their feat against the Egyptian government.</p>
<blockquote>
<p>He offered Iran information about an Egyptian government plan to storm several islands in the Persian Gulf that both Iran and the United Arab Emirates lay claim to. According to Mohammed, in return for this information, the Iranian government paid Zawahiri $2 million and helped train members of al-Jihad in a coup attempt that never actually took place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>However, in public Zawahiri has harshly denounced the Iranian government. In December 2007 he said, "We discovered Iran collaborating with America in its invasions of Afghanistan and Iraq."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lauramansfield_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-lauramansfield-82">[82]</a></sup> In the same video messages, he moreover chides Iran for "repeating the ridiculous joke that says that al-Qaida and the Taliban are agents of America," before playing a video clip in which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ayatollah_Rafsanjani" title="Ayatollah Rafsanjani">Ayatollah Rafsanjani</a> says, "In Afghanistan, they were present in Afghanistan, because of Al-Qa'ida; and the Taliban, who created the Taliban? America is the one who created the Taliban, and America's friends in the region are the ones who financed and armed the Taliban."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lauramansfield_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-lauramansfield-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Zawahiri's criticism of Iran's government continues when he states,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Despite Iran's repetition of the slogan 'Death to America, death to Israel,' we haven't heard even one Fatwa from one Shiite authority, whether in Iran or elsewhere, calling for Jihad against the Americans in Iraq and Afghanistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lauramansfield_82-2"><a href="#cite_note-lauramansfield-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Zawahiri has dismissed that there is any cooperation between Iran and Al Qaeda against their common enemy, to wit, the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> He also said that "Iran Stabbed a Knife into the Back of the Islamic Nation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2008, Zawahiri blamed Iranian state media and <a href="/wiki/Al-Manar" title="Al-Manar">Al-Manar</a> for perpetuating the "lie" that "there are no heroes among the Sunnis who can hurt America as no-one else did in history" in order to discredit the Al Qaeda network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Zawahiri was referring to some <a href="/wiki/9/11_conspiracy_theories" title="9/11 conspiracy theories">9/11 conspiracy theories</a> according to which Al Qaeda was not responsible for the 9/11 attacks.</p>
<p>On the seventh anniversary of the attacks of September 11, 2001, Zawahiri released a 90-minute tape<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com-86">[86]</a></sup> in which he blasted "the guardian of Muslims in Tehran" for recognizing "the two hireling governments"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iht.com_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-iht.com-87">[87]</a></sup> in Iraq and Afghanistan.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_activities_in_Russia">Alleged activities in Russia</span></h3>
<p>There have been doubts as to the true nature of al-Zawahiri's encounter with the Russians in 1996. Washington, D.C.-based <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Foundation" title="Jamestown Foundation">Jamestown Foundation</a> scholar <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Evgenii_Novikov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Evgenii Novikov (page does not exist)">Evgenii Novikov</a> has argued that it seems unlikely that the Russians would not have been able to determine who he was, given their well-trained Arabists and the obviously suspicious act of Muslims crossing illegally a border with multiple false identities and encrypted documents in Arabic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Assassinated former FSB agent <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Litvinenko" title="Alexander Litvinenko">Alexander Litvinenko</a> alleged, among other things, that during this time, al-Zawahiri was indeed being trained by the FSB,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and that he was not the only link between al-Qaeda and the FSB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a> officer, speaker on the <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a> and writer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Konstantin_Preobrazhenskiy" title="Konstantin Preobrazhenskiy">Konstantin Preobrazhenskiy</a> supported Litvinenko's claim and said that Litvinenko "was responsible for securing the secrecy of Al-Zawahiri's arrival in Russia, who was trained by FSB instructors in <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, Northern Caucasus, in 1996–1997."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_in_Egypt">Activities in Egypt</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/November_1997_Luxor_massacre" title="November 1997 Luxor massacre">November 1997 Luxor massacre</a></div>
<p>While there Zawahiri learned of a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Gama%27a_al-Islamiyya#Nonviolence_Initiative" title="Al-Gama'a al-Islamiyya">Nonviolence Initiative</a>" being organized in Egypt to end the terror campaign that had killed hundreds and resulting government crackdown that had imprisoned thousands. Zawahiri angrily opposed this "surrender" in letters to the London newspaper <i>Al-Sharq al-Awsat</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Together with members of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Gama%27a_al-Islamiyya" title="Al-Gama'a al-Islamiyya">al-Gama'a al-Islamiyya</a>, he helped organize a massive attack on tourists at the Temple of Hatshepsut to sabotage the initiative by provoking the government into repression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The attack by six men dressed in police uniforms succeeded in machine-gunning and hacking to death 58 foreign tourists and four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_people" title="Egyptian people">Egyptians</a>, including "a five-year-old British child and four Japanese couples on their honeymoons," and devastated the Egyptian tourist industry for a number of years. Nonetheless the Egyptian reaction was not what Zawahiri had hoped for. The attack so stunned and angered Egyptian society that Islamists denied responsibility. Zawahiri blamed the police for the killing, but also held the tourists responsible for their own deaths for coming to Egypt,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The people of Egypt consider the presence of these foreign tourists to be aggression against Muslims and Egypt... The young men are saying that this is our country and not a place for frolicking and enjoyment, especially for you.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The massacre was so unpopular that no terror attacks occurred in Egypt for several years thereafter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="more precision needed; if opinion, needs attribution; replace several by a number (May 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Zawahiri was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_penalty" title="Death penalty">sentenced to death</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Trial_in_absentia" title="Trial in absentia">in absentia</a></i> in 1999 by an Egyptian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_tribunal" title="Military tribunal">military tribunal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_and_whereabouts_after_the_September_11_attacks">Activities and whereabouts after the September 11 attacks</span></h3>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>...The second power depends on God alone, then on its wide popularity and alliance with other jihad movements throughout the Islamic nation, from Chechnya in the north to Somalia in the south and from "Eastern Turkestan in the east to Morocco in the west.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— <i>Knights Under the Prophet's Banner: Meditations on the Jihadist Movement", Released by Al-Sharq Al-Awsat, originally written by Al-Qaeda leader Ayman al-Zawahiri in 2001<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aaron2008_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aaron2008-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NA2002_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-NA2002-99">[99]</a></sup></i></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>...It seeks revenge against the gang-leaders of global unbelief, the United States, Russia, and Israel. It demands the blood price for the martyrs, the mothers' grief, the deprived orphans, the suffering prisoners, and the torments of those who are tortured everywhere in the Islamic lands―from Turkistan in the east to Andalusia.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— <i>Knights Under the Prophet's Banner: Meditations on the Jihadist Movement", Released by Al-Sharq Al-Awsat, originally written by Al-Qaeda leader Ayman al-Zawahiri in 2001<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kepel2004_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kepel2004-100">[100]</a></sup></i></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>...It also gave young Muslim mujahidin―Arabs, Pakistanis, Turks, and Muslims from Central and East Asia―a great opportunity to get acquainted with each other on the land of Afghan jihad through their comradeship-at-arms against the enemies of Islam.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— <i>Knights Under the Prophet's Banner: Meditations on the Jihadist Movement", Released by Al-Sharq Al-Awsat, originally written by Al-Qaeda leader Ayman al-Zawahiri in 2001<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RubinRubin2004_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-RubinRubin2004-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LinschotenKuehn2012_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-LinschotenKuehn2012-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Devji2005_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Devji2005-103">[103]</a></sup></i></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="1280" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg/220px-Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg/330px-Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg/440px-Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hamid_Mir_interviewing_Osama_bin_Laden_and_Ayman_al-Zawahiri_2001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> sits with his adviser al-Zawahiri during an interview with Pakistani journalist <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Mir" title="Hamid Mir">Hamid Mir</a>, in November 2001.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In December 2001, al-Zawahiri published the book <i>Knights Under the Prophet's Banner</i> outlining al-Qaeda's ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> English translations of this book were published; excerpts are available online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">U.S. invasion of Afghanistan</a>, al-Zawahiri's whereabouts are unknown, but he is generally thought to be in tribal Pakistan. Although he releases videos of himself frequently <i>(see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Messages_of_Ayman_al-Zawahiri" title="Messages of Ayman al-Zawahiri">Messages of Ayman al-Zawahiri</a>)</i>, al-Zawahiri did not appear alongside bin Laden in any of them after 2003. In 2003, it was rumored that he was under arrest in Iran, although this was later discovered to be false.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In 2004, the Pakistan Army launched an aggressive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_wana" title="Battle of wana">operation</a> in Wana, Pakistan. Reports began to surface that he was trapped in the center of the conflict by the army. But when, after weeks of fighting, the army captured the area, it was later revealed that he either escaped or was never among the fighters. As the conflict spread into the tribal areas of western Pakistan, Ayman al-Zawahiri became a prime target of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISI_(Pakistan)" title="ISI (Pakistan)">ISI</a>'s Directorate for Joint Counterintelligence Bureau (J-COIN Bureau). However, despite a series of operations they were unable to capture him.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reward_for_Osama_bin_Laden,_Ayman_al_Zawahiri_--_AFD290B.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="211" data-file-width="400" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Reward_for_Osama_bin_Laden%2C_Ayman_al_Zawahiri_--_AFD290B.jpg/300px-Reward_for_Osama_bin_Laden%2C_Ayman_al_Zawahiri_--_AFD290B.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Reward_for_Osama_bin_Laden%2C_Ayman_al_Zawahiri_--_AFD290B.jpg 1.5x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reward_for_Osama_bin_Laden,_Ayman_al_Zawahiri_--_AFD290B.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. propaganda leaflet used in Afghanistan, with bin Laden and Ayman al-Zawahiri</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On January 13, 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a>, aided by Pakistan's ISI, launched an <a href="/wiki/Damadola_airstrike" title="Damadola airstrike">airstrike on Damadola</a>, a Pakistani village near the Afghan border where they believed al-Zawahiri was located. The airstrike was supposed to kill al-Zawahiri and this was reported in international news over the following days. Many victims of the airstrike were buried without being identified. Anonymous U.S. government officials claimed that some terrorists were killed and the Bajaur tribal area government confirmed that at least four terrorists were among the dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Anti-American protests broke out around the country and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistani_government" title="Pakistani government">Pakistani government</a> condemned the U.S. attack and the loss of innocent life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> On January 30, a new video was released showing al-Zawahiri unhurt. The video discussed the airstrike, but did not reveal if al-Zawahiri was present in the village at that time.</p>
<p>On August 1, 2008, <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> reported that it had obtained a copy of an intercepted letter dated July 29, 2008, from unnamed sources in Pakistan, which urgently requested a doctor to treat al-Zawahiri. The letter indicated that al-Zawahiri was critically injured in a US missile strike at Azam Warsak village in South Waziristan on July 28 that also reportedly killed al Qaeda explosives expert <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_Khabab_al-Masri" title="Abu Khabab al-Masri">Abu Khabab al-Masri</a>. Taliban Mehsud spokesman <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maulvi_Umar" title="Maulvi Umar">Maulvi Umar</a> told the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> on August 2, 2008, that the report of al-Zawahiri's injury was false.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early September 2008, Pakistan Army claimed that they "almost" captured al-Zawahiri after getting information that he and his wife were in the <a href="/wiki/Mohmand_Agency" title="Mohmand Agency">Mohmand Agency</a>, in northwest Pakistan. After raiding the area, officials didn't find him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCTnotdead_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCTnotdead-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2013, al-Zawahiri arbitrated against the merger of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq" title="Islamic State of Iraq">Islamic State of Iraq</a> with the Syrian-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabhat_al-Nusra" title="Jabhat al-Nusra">Jabhat al-Nusra</a> into <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> as was declared in April by <a href="/wiki/Abu_Bakr_al-Baghdadi" title="Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi">Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abu_Mohammad_al-Julani" title="Abu Mohammad al-Julani">Abu Mohammad al-Julani</a>, leader of al-Nusra Front, affirmed the group's allegiance to al-Qaeda and al-Zawahiri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2015, Zawahiri urged Islamic State (ISIL) to stop fighting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front" title="Al-Nusra Front">al-Nusra Front</a>, the official al-Qaeda affiliate in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> and to unite with all other jihadists against the supposed alliance between America, Russia, Europe, <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shiites</a> and Iran, and Bashar al-Assad’s <a href="/wiki/Alawites" title="Alawites">Alawite</a> regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ayman al-Zawahiri released a statement supporting <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_conflict" title="Xinjiang conflict">jihad in Xinjiang</a> against Chinese, <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_the_North_Caucasus" title="Insurgency in the North Caucasus">jihad in the Caucasus against the Russians</a> and naming Somalia, Yemen, Syria, Iraq and Afghanistan as battlegrounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Zawahiri endorsed "jihad to liberate every span of land of the Muslims that has been usurped and violated, from <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashgar</a> to <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, and from the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> to <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Uyghurs inhabit Kashgar, the city which was mentioned by Zawahiri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In another statement he said, "My mujahideen brothers in all places and of all groups ... we face aggression from America, Europe, and Russia ... so it's up to us to stand together as one from East Turkestan to Morocco".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> In 2015 the <a href="/wiki/Turkistan_Islamic_Party" title="Turkistan Islamic Party">Turkistan Islamic Party</a> (East Turkistan Islamic Movement) released an image showing Al Qaeda leaders Ayman al Zawahiri and Osama Bin Laden meeting with <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Mahsum" title="Hasan Mahsum">Hasan Mahsum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Uyghurs <a href="/wiki/East_Turkestan_independence_movement" title="East Turkestan independence movement">East Turkestan independence movement</a> was endorsed in the serial "Islamic Spring”'s 9th release by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ayman_Al-Zawahiri" title="Ayman Al-Zawahiri">Ayman Al-Zawahiri</a>, the chief of Al-Qaeda. Zawahiri confirmed that the Afghanistan war after 9/11 included the participation of Uighurs and that the jihadists like Zarwaqi, Bin Ladin and the Uyghur <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Mahsum" title="Hasan Mahsum">Hasan Mahsum</a> were provided with refuge together in Afghanistan under Taliban rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Uyghur fighters were praised by Zawahiri, before a Turkistan Islamic Party performed a <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a> bombing on 30 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Doğu Türkistan Bülteni Haber Ajansı reported that the Uyghur <a href="/wiki/Turkistan_Islamic_Party" title="Turkistan Islamic Party">Turkistan Islamic Party</a> was praised by <a href="/wiki/Abu_Qatada" title="Abu Qatada">Abu Qatada</a> along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdul_Razzaq_al_Mahdi" title="Abdul Razzaq al Mahdi">Abdul Razzaq al Mahdi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maqdisi" title="Maqdisi">Maqdisi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhaysini" title="Muhaysini">Muhaysini</a> and Zawahiri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Abu Muhammad al-Maqdisi and Abu Qatada were referenced by Muhaysini. Al-Qaeda leaders Osama bin Laden and Ayman al Zawahiri were lauded by Muhaysini.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Presently, the <a href="/wiki/Rewards_for_Justice_Program" title="Rewards for Justice Program">Rewards for Justice Program</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. Department of State</a> is offering a reward of up to <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>25 million for information about his location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FBI_Al-Zawahiri_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-FBI_Al-Zawahiri-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfj_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-rfj-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliations">Affiliations</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a> at age 14</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">Last Emir</a> of <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">Egyptian Islamic Jihad</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cairo_University" title="Cairo University">Cairo University</a> Alumni</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Crescent Movement</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Views">Views</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loyalty_and_enmity">Loyalty and enmity</span></h3>
<p>In a lengthy treatise titled "Loyalty and Enmity", Zawahiri argues that Muslims must at all times be loyal to Islam and to one another, while hating or at least being clean from everything and everyone outside of Islam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Female_combatants">Female combatants</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sex_segregation_and_Islam" title="Sex segregation and Islam">Sex segregation and Islam</a></div>
<p>Zawahiri has said in an interview that the group does not have women combatants and that a woman's role is limited to caring for the homes and children of al-Qaeda fighters. This resulted in a debate regarding the role of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mujahid" title="Mujahid">mujahid</a> women like <a href="/wiki/Sajida_Mubarak_Atrous_al-Rishawi" title="Sajida Mubarak Atrous al-Rishawi">Sajida Mubarak Atrous al-Rishawi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotional_activities">Promotional activities</span></h2>
<p>Zawahiri places supreme importance on winning public support, and castigated <a href="/wiki/Abu_Musab_al-Zarqawi" title="Abu Musab al-Zarqawi">Abu Musab al-Zarqawi</a> in this regard: "In the absence of this popular support the Islamic mujahid movement would be crushed in the shadows."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_and_audio_messages">Video and audio messages</span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
