<b style="text-align: center;"><i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Author:Ayman_al-Zawahiri" title="s:Author:Ayman al-Zawahiri">Ayman al-Zawahiri</a></i></b></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Videos_of_Ayman_al-Zawahiri" title="Videos of Ayman al-Zawahiri">Videos of Ayman al-Zawahiri</a></div>
<ul>
<li>May 2003: Tape was broadcast by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Jazeera" title="Al-Jazeera">al-Jazeera</a> and included the directives (interpreted) "Raze/Singe the floor out from under their feet ... the political and corporate interests of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> ... and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>", which caused a global lockdown and extensive confusion for Norway.</li>
<li>Early September 2003: A video showing al-Zawahiri and <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">bin Laden</a> walking together, as well as an audiotape, is released to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Jazeera" title="Al-Jazeera">al-Jazeera</a> network.</li>
<li>September 9, 2004: Another video is released announcing more assaults.</li>
<li>August 4, 2005: al-Zawahiri issues a televised statement blaming <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and his government's foreign policy for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/July_2005_London_bombings" title="July 2005 London bombings">July 2005 London bombings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 1, 2005: al-Jazeera broadcasts a video message from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohammed_Sidique_Khan" title="Mohammed Sidique Khan">Mohammed Sidique Khan</a>, one of bombers of the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a>. His message is followed by another message from al-Zawahiri, blaming again Tony Blair for the 7/7 bombings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 19, 2005: al-Zawahiri claims responsibility for the London bombings and dismisses U.S. efforts in Afghanistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 7, 2005: The full 40-minute interview from September is posted on the Internet with previously unseen video footage. See below for links.</li>
<li>April 3, 2008: al-Zawahiri said that <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> doesn't kill innocents and that its [former] leader Osama bin Laden is healthy. The questions asked his views about <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 22, 2008: An audio interview in which, among other subjects, al-Zawahiri attacks the Shiite Iran and Hezbollah for blaming the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">9/11 attacks</a> on <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, and thus discrediting al-Qaeda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></li>
<li>On the 7th anniversary of the attacks of September 11, 2001, al-Zawahiri released a 90-minute tape,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com-86">[86]</a></sup> in which he blasted "the guardian of <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>" for "the two hireling governments"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iht.com_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-iht.com-87">[87]</a></sup> in Iraq and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>.</li>
<li>January 7, 2009: An audio message released, where al-Zawahiri vows revenge for Israel's air and ground assault on Gaza and calls the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> state's actions against Hamas militants "a gift" from U.S. President-elect <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> for the recent uprising conflict in Gaza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></li>
<li>June 2, 2009: Audio messages claiming that Barack Obama is not welcome in Egypt.</li>
<li>July 15, 2009: al-Zawahiri urges <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistani_people" title="Pakistani people">Pakistanis</a> to support the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a>.</li>
<li>October 4, 2009: <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that al-Zawahiri had asserted that <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> had tortured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_Al_Sheikh_Al_Libi" title="Ibn Al Sheikh Al Libi">Ibn Al Sheikh Al Libi</a> to death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes2009-10-04_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes2009-10-04-141">[141]</a></sup> Al Libi was a key source the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_President" title="United States President">Presidency</a> had claimed established that Iraq had provided training to al-Qaeda in Iraq's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_of_Mass_Destruction" title="Weapons of Mass Destruction">Weapons of Mass Destruction</a>.</li>
<li>December 14, 2009: In an audio recording released on December 14, 2009, al-Zawahiri renewed calls to establish an Islamic state in Israel and urged his followers to “seek jihad against Jews” and their supporters. He also called for jihad against America and the West, and labeled Egyptian president Hosni Mubarak, King Abdullah II of Jordan, and King Abdullah bin Abdulaziz of Saudi Arabia as the “brothers of Satan”.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></li>
<li>June 8, 2011: al-Zawahiri released his first video since the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden" title="Death of Osama bin Laden">death of Osama bin Laden</a>, praising bin Laden and warning the U.S. of reprisal attacks, but without staking a claim on the leadership of al-Qaeda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 3, 2014: In a 55-minute-long video, al-Zawahiri announced the formation of a new wing called <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Indian_Subcontinent" title="Al-Qaeda in the Indian Subcontinent">al-Qaeda in the Indian Subcontinent</a> (AQIS), which would wage jihad "to liberate its land, to restore its sovereignty, and to revive its Caliphate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndiaAlQaeda_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-IndiaAlQaeda-144">[144]</a></sup> Reaction amongst Muslims in India to the formation of the new wing was one of fury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndiaGazette_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-IndiaGazette-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li>In late August, 2016: A Jihadi website released series of sermons by al-Zawahiri regarding Jihad.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_Q.26A">Online Q&amp;A</span></h3>
<p>In mid-December 2007, al-Zawahiri's spokespeople announced plans for an "open interview" on a handful of Islamic Web sites. The administrators of 4 known <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jihadist" title="Jihadist">jihadist</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Web_sites" title="Web sites">web sites</a> have been authorized to collect and forward questions, "unedited", they pledge, and "regardless of whether they are in support of or are against" <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>, which would be forwarded to al-Zawahiri on January 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> al-Zawahiri responded to the questions later in 2008; among the things he said were that al-Qaeda didn't kill innocents, and that al-Qaeda would move to target <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> "after expelling the occupier from <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span></h3>

</ul>
